Mr. Preston, from the Committee on Roads and Canals, reported the following bill: A Bill To provide for taking care of the Louisville and Portland Canal, and to prevent the same from falling into bad repair. Whereas the legislature of the commonwealth of Kentucky, by an act passed the twenty-first of January, eighteen hundred and forty-two, authorized the Louisville and Portland Canal Company to appropriate the net income of the company in purchasing the shares other than those owned by the United States, until the United States should be the sole owner of the stock of said company; and whereas it appears the United States will, under said arrangement, become the sole owner of said stock before the next session of Congress, and it is necessary to provide for the custody and preservation of the public property aforesaid, and to provide the proper officers to take charge and custody of the same, so that the commerce and navigation of the Ohio may not be obstructed, and that said canal may not fall into decay or bad repair--therefore,","Committee on Roads and Canals"

"llhb","033","17150002.tif","033","001","h","2","H.R. 515","18540803","",""
"llhb","033","17160000.tif","033","001","h","","H.R. 516","18540803","Read twice, and committed to a Committee of the Whole House on the state of the Union. Mr. John G. Davis, from the Committee for the District of Columbia, reported the following bill: A Bill To authorize the extension, construction, and use of the Metropolitan Railroad Company, into and within the District of Columbia. Whereas by an act of the Congress of the United States, approved March third, eighteen hundred and fifty-three, and entitled ''An act to incorporate the Georgetown and Catoctin Railroad Company,'' it was provided that whenever the State of Maryland should by law incorporate a company to lay out and construct a railroad from any point, in connexion with the Baltimore and Ohio railroad, at or near the Point of Rocks, to Georgetown, in the District of Columbia, the right of way, not exceeding sixty-six feet wide, should be and was thereby, granted to such company; and whereas the general assembly of the State of Maryland did afterwards, on the fifth day of May, eighteen hundred and fifty-three, pass an act entitled ''An act to incorporate the Metropolitan Railroad Company,'' which originated in the design to meet the terms and conditions of said act of Congress, but which, as finally passed, provided for the incorporation of a company to construct and repair a railroad from Georgetown, in the District of Columbia, through the counties of Montgomery, Frederick, and Washington, in the State of Maryland, to Hagerstown, in said State, crossing the Baltimore and Ohio railroad at a point not further than five miles from the Monocacy viaduct by the line of said railroad, not exceeding sixty-six feet wide, and with as many sets of tracks as the president and directors, or a majority of them, might deem necessary; and whereas a company has been organized under said act of assembly, and has applied to Congress for a law authorizing and enabling it to exercise its chartered powers within the District of Columbia and to conduct its said road into and through said District: Therefore--","Committee for the District of Columbia"

"llhb","033","17210000.tif","033","002","h","","H.R. 516","18541221","Read twice and referred to the Committee on the District of Columbia. An Act To authorize the extension, construction, and use, of the Metropolitan Railroad Company into and within the District of Columbia. Whereas, by an act of the Congress of the United States, approved March third, eighteen hundred and fifty-three, and entitled ''An act to incorporate the Georgetown and Catoctin Railroad Company,'' it was provided that whenever the State of Maryland should by law incorporate a company to lay out and construct a railroad from any point, in connexion with the Baltimore and Ohio railroad, at or near the Point of Rocks, to Georgetown, in the District of Columbia, the right of way not exceeding sixty-six feet wide, should be, and was thereby, granted to such company; and whereas the general assembly of the State of Maryland did afterwards, on the fifth day of May, eighteen hundred and fifty-three, pass an act entitled ''An act to incorporate the Metropolitan Railroad Company,'' which originated in the design to meet the terms and conditions of said act of Congress, but which, as finally passed, provided for the incorporation of a company to construct and repair a railroad from Georgetown, in the District of Columbia, through the counties of Montgomery, Frederick, and Washington, in the State of Maryland, to Hagerstown, in said State, crossing the Baltimore and Ohio railroad at a point not further than five miles from the Monocacy viaduct by the line of said railroad, not exceeding sixty-six feet wide, and with as many sets of tracks as the president and directors, or a majority of them, might deem necessary; and whereas a company has been organized under said act of assembly, and has applied to Congress for a law authorizing and enabling it to exercise its chartered powers within the District of Columbia, and to conduct its said road into and through said district. Therefore--","Committee on the District of Columbia"

"llhb","033","26910000.tif","033","002","h","","H.R. 740","18550208","Read twice, and committed to a Committee of the Whole House to-morrow. Mr. Kerr, from the Committee on the Judiciary, reported the following bill: A Bill For the relief of assignees of Anthony De St. Maxent. Whereas the government of the United States has entered upon certain lands in the State of Louisiana which were granted by Baron Carondelet, governor general of the Territory of Orleans, to Anthony De St. Maxent, by his grant dated the day of, seventeen hundred and ninety-five, and has erected thereon buildings and fortifications which, with the grounds used as appurtenant thereto, are called and known as ''Fort Jackson,'' on the western bank of the Mississippi river; And whereas the lands so appropriated to the military use of the government were, at the time of such appropriation, the private property of the assignees of Anthony De St. Maxent, and were so appropriated under and by virtue of the power reserved by the King of Spain in the third article of said original grant; And whereas it is the duty of the government to make full compensation to the owners of said lands for all loss and damage to them by, from, or through such military and public use of their property, according to the spirit and effect of the constitution of the United States; Therefore,","Committee on the Judiciary"
